mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: 189.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;">Constitution of Bangladesh, 1972</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: 189.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;">Article 102</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: 189.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;">Legitimate Expectation:</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: 189.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;">The High Court Division observed that from the records it appeared that initially on 20.08.2015 the Bank’s Board of Directors (BoD) at its 435<sup>th</sup> meeting decided to recruit in the post of ‘Senior Officer’, ‘Officer’ and Officer (Cash)’ as per vacancies arising on 31.12.2014 according to rankings in a merit list. This led to communication BANK and forth between the Banks’s BoD and the Ministry of Finance seeing the latter’s approval of appointments in the vacancies. Significantly, in its communication of 01.09.2015 to the Ministry, the Bank confirmed, inter alia, that the merit list itself had a validity period till 13.08.2015. Hence the applicants, though successful, cannot remain in expectation of being appointed after that date. <span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">  </span>14</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: 189.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: 189.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;">Evidence Act (I of 1872)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: 189.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;">Section 115</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: 189.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;">The advertisement in response to which the petitioners applied was for a finite number of vacancies. Once those vacancies are filled in there cannot be any expectation that the candidates who were successful in the examination would automatically be appointed in any future recruitment drive. We do not find that any such assurance was given by the authorities.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                         </span>13</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span></span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.5in; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.1pt;">For the Petitioner </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.1pt; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;">(in CP No.161, 716 and 717 of 18)</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.1pt;">: </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.1pt; mso-bidi-language: EN-US; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;">For Respondent Nos.1-6</span></strong> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.1pt; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;">(in CP No.161 of ’18</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.1pt;">: </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.1pt; mso-bidi-language: EN-US; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Mr. Mahbubey Alam, learned Attorney General instructed by Mr. Haridas Paul, Advocate-on-Record</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.5in; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.1pt; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;">For Respondent No.7</span></strong> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.1pt; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;">(in CP No.161 of ’18)</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.1pt;">: </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.1pt; mso-bidi-language: EN-US; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Mr. Shamim Khaled Ahmed, Senior Advocate instructed by Shirin Afroz, Advocate-on-Record</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.5in; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;">For Respondent No.8</span></strong> <strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;">(in CP No.161 of ’18)</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">:</span></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Mr. Sheik Fazle Noor Taposh, Advocate with Mohammad Mehedi Hasan Chowdhury, Advocate and Mr. Sheik Zakir Hossain, Advocate instructed by Mr. Nurul Islam Chowdhury, Advocate-on-Record</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.5in; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;">For the Respondents</span></strong><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">: </span></strong><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;">(in CP No.397 of ’18)</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">:</span></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Mr. Mahbubey Alam, Senior Advocate with Mr. Sheik Zakir Hossain, Advocate instructed by Mr. Nurul Islam Chowdhury, Advocate-on-Record</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.5in; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;">For the Respondents</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">: (in CP No.699 and 716-717 of 18): Mr. Sheik Zakir Hossain, Advocate instructed by Mr. Nurul Islam Chowdhury, <span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span>Advocate-on-Record</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: center; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">JUDGMENT</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><u><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; font-variant: small-caps; mso-ansi-language: EN-GB;">MUHAMMAD IMMAN ALI</span></u></strong><strong><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; font-variant: small-caps;">, J:</span></u></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">These petitions for leave to appeal have been filed against the judgement and order dated the 27<sup>th</sup> day of July, 2017 passed by the High Court Division in Writ Petition No.9356 of 2016 discharging the Rule <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">Nisi</em>.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.2pt; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">                   </span></span></span></em></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.2pt; mso-bidi-language: EN-US; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">The facts, relevant for disposal of these civil petitions for leave to appeal, are that Sonali Bank Ltd. published a recruitment circular dated 27.01.2014 in the Daily Ittefaq and the Financial Express (which was further published in 'Weekly Chakrir Bazaar' on 31.1.2014) inviting applications from eligible candidates for the posts of 'Senior Officer', 'Officer' and 'Officer' (Cash) that would enable the Bank to directly recruit and appoint in the said posts as and when vacancies arose. The last date of submitting applications was 26.02.2014. The writ-petitioners duly applied for the posts advertised in the recruitment circulars upon fulfilling the necessary prerequisites. They received their admit cards and sat for the examinations as per the job circular dated 27.01.2004. The MCQ and written examinations for the posts of Senior Officer, Officer and Officer Cash were held on 22.08.2014 and 13.09.2014 respectively. As the Bankers Selection Committee (BSC) delayed recruitment of the petitioners in the waiting list and published the impugned job circular, they filed Writ Petition No.9356 of 2016 and obtained the Rule <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">Nisi.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">                   </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">The General Manager, Human Resources Development, Sonali Bank (respondent No. 7), filed affidavit-in-opposition contending, <em>inter alia</em>, that the job circulars dated 27.01.2014 were for a total of 1,707 posts and after the <em>viva voce</em> examination Merit lists of 1,508 candidates in the post of Senior Officer, 1,634 candidates in the post of Officer and 2,503 candidates in the post of Officer (Cash) were prepared. It is stated further that out of a total of 1,707 posts, 1,436 candidates were selected for direct recruitment. The Bank clarifies further that due to not having enough candidates in -the "Freedom Fighters Quota" it was not possible to appoint 271 candidates in the same. It is stated that after sending the appointment letters out to 1,436 appointees, 1,306 appointees joined in their respective posts. Among the 40 candidates who had not joined, 8 candidates were in "Freedom Fighters Quota” and subsequently due to non-availability of candidates under the said quota the Bank’s Board of Directors("BOD") on 28.07.2015 decided to recruit candidates against the 32 remaining posts where 25 candidates were in merit quota, 4 were in district quota, two were in female quota and 1 was from tribal quota and the said decision was approved at the BOD's 436<sup>th</sup> Meeting of 05.08.2015. The said decision was conveyed to respondent No.7, being the Bank's Deputy General Manager, Human Resources Development Department on 06.08.2015. This, the Bank submits, goes to show that the said 32 candidates were appointed only against the posts which could not be filled by the otherwise directly selected candidates and states in reiteration that the said posts were among those covered by the circular of January, 2014.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.2pt; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">                   </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.2pt; mso-bidi-language: EN-US; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Before the High Court Division, it was submitted on behalf of the Bank that the statements made in the said writ petition that the writ-petitioners were supposed to be recruited from a "Panel List" is absolutely imaginary, vague, baseless and misconceived. It was asserted that there was nothing, in the job circulars that even remotely suggested the prospects of any panel or waiting list permitting of an available pool of prospective recruitees. The Bank's position generally is that it only appointed the successful candidates from the merit list in the vacant posts and that the impugned job circulars published on 22.02.2016 are for completely new posts other than the ones advertised on 27.01.2014. In the circumstances, therefore, the Bank sees no automatic right arising in favour of the writ-petitioners to be recruited for the new posts <span style="mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">at</span> any future date.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">                   </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Writ-respondent No.7 further contended that there was nothing included in the job circular dated 27.01.2014 that ‘a panel’ or ‘waiting list’ would be prepared for future recruitment in the posts of Senior Officer, Officer and Officer Cash. He further contended that the idea of preparation and recruitment from such ‘panel’ or ‘waiting list’ was just a fictitious belief of the writ-petitioners. Mere proposal of recommendations made by the concerned authority as reflected in the annexure to the writ petition did not create any legal or vested right in favour of the petitioners to be recruited in the new posts circulated on 22.02.2016 in various dailies. He further contended that the writ-respondents did not provide any unequivocal assurance whether by means of an expressed promise or an established practice that the successful candidates would be recruited for any post created in future from the panel or waiting list.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">                   </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Writ-respondent No.2 by filing affidavit-in-opposition contended that the panel waiting list had validity and the awaiting candidates would be called up if the appointed candidate failed to join, left the post or otherwise the post fell vacant. Under the recruitment circular dated 27.01.2014, the validity period for appointment in the post of Senior Officer, Officer and Officer Cash from the panel waiting list was on 30.06.2015 which was extended till 31.12.2015. The impugned recruitment circular dated 22.02.2016 was published after expiry of the panel waiting list’s validity period and the panel waiting list prepared under a particular recruitment circular was not entitled to be considered in the subsequent recruitment circular. Writ-respondent No.2 further contended that the said panel of Senior Officer, Officer and Officer Cash were prepared by Sonali Bank Limited before formation of BSC and BSC had no jurisdiction to give any suggestion in this regard. The impugned job circular was issued as per decision of the Ministry of Finance.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">                   </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">In due course, after hearing both the parties, by the impugned judgement and order, the Rule was discharged. Hence, the writ-petitioners filed the instant civil petitions for leave to appeal before this Court.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.2pt; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">                   </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.2pt; mso-bidi-language: EN-US; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Dr. Rafiqur Rahman, learned Counsel, appearing for the petitioners submitted that the writ-petitioners had gone through the complete recruitment process and successfully qualified to be recruited for the positions advertised at the relevant time in 2014. The Bank authority had filled up the vacancies as per merit list from the qualified candidates. Subsequently, they prepared a waiting panel list with the successfully qualified candidates including the petitioners for the purpose of filling up the vacancies in future. The long time practice and custom of the state-owned Banks and other financial institutions is that the recruitment in the upcoming vacant positions is always filled up from the waiting panel list. Thereby, the writ-petitioners had a legitimate expectation to be recruited in the post of Senior Officer, Officer and Officer Cash in Sonali Bank Limited. He further submitted that in all the circulars pre-formation of the Bankers Selection Committee, did not contain any word that a Panel or Waiting List would be prepared with the successful candidates but it was a regular practice to form the said Panel or Waiting List for filling up the upcoming vacancies. The writ-respondents have already acted on the said tradition or practice and cannot deny without giving <span style="mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">prior</span> notice to the writ-petitioners. Hence the impugned judgement and order dated 27.07.2017 is liable to be set aside. He further submitted that the High Court Division failed to consider the fact that customs are also recognised as having force of law as per article 152 of the Constitution of the People’s Republic of Bangladesh. Considering the definition of law in the said article, the High Court Division should have made the Rule absolute and as <span style="mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">such</span><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">, </em><span style="mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">the impugned judgement and order dated 27.07.2017 is liable to be </span>set aside. He further submitted that the High Court Division failed to appreciate that admittedly the list prepared by the respondents had not been made public by way <span style="mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">of</span> publishing the same in any manner. The petitioners own source gathered information about the said list. Once a List is prepared with the successfully qualified candidates to fill up specific vacancies the respondents cannot refuse to appoint them whimsically in those posts when vacancy exists. Due to the promise of the respondents, the petitioners relied upon their promise and they had been waiting to be appointed in the vacant posts and in the meantime, most of them have crossed the age limit to get appointment in the civil service. The High Court Division without considering the above facts and circumstances arrived at an erroneous conclusion of the case and as such, the impugned judgement and order dated 27.07.2017 is liable to be set aside. He further submitted that the High Court Division failed to appreciate that the respondents have promised to the petitioners that they will be recruited as and when vacancy occurs in the future and accordingly there had been vacancies in the aforesaid three posts, but respondent No.2 without considering the demand of the petitioners had published the job circulars dated 22.02.2016 which is apparent violation of the established “principle of estoppel” from going back on their earlier promise. He farther submitted that the petitioners had a legitimate expectation that they will be recruited in the aforesaid three posts, but respondent No.2 most arbitrarily and illegally published the impugned job circulars dated 22.02.2016 with an intention to fill up the vacancies excluding the petitioners who are on the waiting panel list. It is a settled principle that judicial review may be allowed on the plea of frustration of legitimate expectation in five specific situations: (i) if there is a promise by the authority expressed either by their representation or conduct, (ii) the decision of the authority was arbitrary or unreasonable <span style="mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">within the</span> Wednesbury <span style="mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">principle</span>, (i<span style="mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">ii)there was a failure on the part of the concerned authority to act fairly in taking the decision, (iv) the expectation </span>to be crystallized into a legitimate one, it must be based on clear facts and circumstances leading to a definite expectation and not a mere anticipation or a wish or hope and also must be reasonable in the circumstances and (v) judicial review may allow such a legitimate expectation and quash the impugned decision even in the absence of a strict legal right unless there is an overriding public interest to defeat such an expectation. In the present case, the above observation falls squarely in favour of the petitioners and as such, the impugned judgement and order dated 27.07.2017 is liable to be set aside. He farther submitted that the petitioners have already crossed their age limit to apply for public service while waiting to be recruited in the aforesaid three posts. The policy of the Government in the present era cannot be of ignoring the public interest. If the respondents are allowed to proceed with the recruitment in the aforesaid post of Senior Officer, Officer and Officer Cash then the petitioners will be nowhere with their lives and will suffer irreparable loss and injury and hence all farther <span style="mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">actions on the basis</span> of the <span style="mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">impugned</span> job circular dated 22.02.2016 should be stayed for ends of justice. He further submitted that the petitioners will be highly prejudiced if their right to have equal opportunity in the public service is denied only on technical ground. There are instances in other state-owned banks and financial institutions wherein the validity of the Panel is extended from time to time to facilitate the respective banks to fill up the upcoming vacancies to meet their urgent need. There is no specific law or tradition barring extension of the validity period of a Panel or Waiting List. At the same time, it cannot be decided whimsically to deprive the petitioners from their legitimate right. The High Court Division failed to appreciate the aforesaid aspect of the fact and law and as such the impugned judgement and order is liable to be set aside for ends of justice.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">                   </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Mr. Mahbubey Alam, learned Attorney General appearing for respondent Nos.1-6 in CP Nos.161 and 397 of 2018 supported the impugned judgement and order of the High Court Division.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">               </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Mr. Shamim Khaled, learned Advocate appearing on behalf of respondent No.7 in CP No. 161 of 2018 also supported the impugned judgment and order of the High Court Division.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">               </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Mr. Sheikh Zakir Hossain, learned Advocate appearing on behalf of the respondents in CP Nos.699 and 716-717 of 2018 supported the impugned judgement and order.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">               </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">We have considered the submissions of the learned Advocates appearing on behalf of the respective parties and perused the impugned judgement of the High Court Division and other connected papers on record.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">13.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">               </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">It appears from the judgement of the High Court Division that “the job circular of January, 2014 is silent regarding the creation of “Panels” or “Waiting Lists” and did not provide any unequivocal assurance, whether by means of a promise or an established practice, that the successfully passed candidates who have not been appointed at the initial stage shall nevertheless be appointed to any posts created in the future from any “Panel” or a “Waiting List”. The Merit List that the Respondents have relied upon in the facts for their internal purposes is instead, and in contradiction to the notion of “Panel” or “Waiting List”, found by the High Court Division to be an integral part of any fair and transparent evaluation<a name="bookmark0"></a> and selection process leading to appointments based purely on merit.” The High Court Division observed that the merit list in question in the facts was found to have lost all efficacy beyond 13.08.2015, i.e. its declared and recorded validity period. The High Court Division found that upon filling up of posts as initially remained vacant due to the non-acceptance of appointments by directly selected candidates against advertised posts, the merit list ceased to have all efficacy.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">14.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">               </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">On perusal of the materials on record, we do not find anything to suggest that any indication was given to the intending applicants that they would be included in a “Panel” or “Waiting List” and would be considered for recruitment in the future. The advertisement in response to which the petitioners applied was for a finite number of vacancies. Once those vacancies are filled in there cannot be any expectation that the candidates who were successful in the examination would automatically be appointed in any future recruitment drive. We do not find that any such assurance was given by the authorities.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">15.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">               </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">The High Court Division observed that from the records it appeared that initially on 20.08.2015 the Bank's Board of Directors (BoD) at its 435<sup>th</sup> meeting decided to recruit in the post of ‘Senior Officer’, ‘Officer’ and ‘Officer (Cash)’ as per <span style="mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">vacancies </span>arising on 31.12.2014 according to rankings in a merit list. This led to communications back and forth between the Bank’s BOD and the Ministry of Finance seeking the latter's approval of appointments in the vacancies. Significantly, in its communication of 01.09.2015 to the Ministry, the Bank confirmed, <em>inter</em> <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">alia</em>, that the merit list itself had a validity period till 13.08.2015. Hence, the applicants, though successful, cannot remain in expectation of being appointed after that date.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">16.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">               </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>In view of the discussion above, we do not find any illegality or impropriety in the</span><span style="font-size: 11pt;">impugned judgement and order of the High Court Division.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">17.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">               </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Accordingly, all the civil petitions for leave to appeal are dismissed.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-indent: .5in;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-indent: .5in;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Ed.</span></strong></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><a href="file:///C:/Users/User/AppData/Local/Temp/Rar$DIa7196.2057/Issue__December_19__C.%20P.%20161%20of%2018__Muhammad%20Imman%20Ali_J___AD___2.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: EN-US; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">CIVIL PETITION FOR LEAVE TO APPEAL NO.161 of 2018 WITH CP NOS.397, 699, 716-17 OF 2018</span></u></strong></a><strong><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">. </span></u></strong><span style="font-size: 9.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.2pt; mso-bidi-language: EN-US; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">(From the judgement and order dated the 27<sup>th</sup> day of July, 2017 passed by the High Court Division in Writ Petition No.9356 of 2016)</span></p></div></div></div></div>
820	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Mohammad Ashraf U. Bhu.Vs. Govt. of Bangladesh and ors.</h2>

Petitioner </span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: center; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>(In C.P.No.3126 of 2015)</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: center; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">-Versus-</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">A. Respondents.</span></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 7.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Muslim Marriages and Divorce (Registration) Act (LII of 1974)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Section 4</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: 189.0pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">When any person is appointed as a Nikah Registrar for any local area, his service will continue as such until and unless he is disqualified under the law.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">   </span>...13</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Muslim Marriages and Divorce (Registration) Act (LII of 1974)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Section 4</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: 189.0pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">A Nikah Registrar, who had been appointed as such for a number of Wards, cannot have all the wards taken away from him. The power of the Government is to curtail his jurisdiction, in other words to appoint a Nikah Registrar for any of the Wards but that power does not extend to totally eliminating his licence as Nikah Registrar, unless there is some other legitimate ground.</span></strong><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                 </span>...15</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span></span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.5in; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.1pt;">For the Petitioner </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.1pt;">(In C.P.No. 2901 of 2015): </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.1pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Mr.Probir Neogi, Senior Advocate with Mr. Mohammad Hossain, Advocate, instructed by Mr. Gias Uddin Ahmed, Advocate-on-Record</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.5in; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">For Respondent No.1 (In both the cases)</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">:</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> <span style="mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Mr. Biswajit Deb Nath, Deputy Attorney General instructed by Mrs. Sufia Khatun, Advocate-on-Record.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.5in; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Respondent Nos.2-10: (In the both Cases)</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">:</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> <span style="mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Not represented</span></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: center; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">JUDGMENT</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><u><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; font-variant: small-caps; mso-ansi-language: EN-GB;">MUHAMMAD IMMAN ALI</span></u></strong><strong><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; font-variant: small-caps;">, J:</span></u></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">These two civil petitions for leave to appeal are directed against the judgement and order dated 19.08.2015 passed by a Division Bench of the High Court Division in Writ Petition No. 12161 of 2013 making the Rule absolute in part directing the respondents to issue Nikah Registration Certificate (sic.)(Nikah Registrar Licence) in favour of the writ petitioner A.S. Md. Siddiqur Rahman for Ward No. 1 under Narayangonj City Corporation within 2(two) months from the date of receipt of the copy of the Judgment and order. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">The facts, relevant for disposal of the civil petitions for leave to appeal, are that the writ petitioner A.S. Md. Siddiqur Rahman was appointed as Nikah Registrar on 13.03.1973 by the Ministry of Law, Justice and Parliamentary Affairs and he was given a licence (mb`) authorizing him to register Mohammedan Marriage and Divorce and perform function as a Quazi within the jurisdiction of Simulpara and Siddhirgonj Union Parishads under P.S. Siddhirgonj, which was at that time within the district of Dhaka. In 2003 one Md. Masihur Rahman was appointed as Nikah Registrar for Simulpara Union Parishad curtailing the jurisdiction of the writ petitioner. In the year 2005 Siddhirgonj Union Parishad was converted into Siddhirgonj Pourasova, comprising five Wards and in the year 2011 Siddhirgonj Pourasova was merged into Narayangonj City Corporation. The writ petitioner was performing his duties as the Nikah Registrar of Ward Nos.1 to 5 under the Narayangonj City Corporation. It is also stated, that on 20.11.2011 respondent No. 5, the Senior Assistant Secretary, Ministry of Law, Justice and Parliamentary Affairs issued a letter directing the writ respondent No. 4, the District Registrar, Narayangonj for sending a panel of Nikah Registrars for Ward Nos. 2 and 7 under the City Corporation. On 24.01.2012 respondent No. 5 directed respondent No. 4 to send panel of Nikah Registrars for Ward No. 3 under the Corporation. Similarly on 26.06.2012 respondent No.5 issued letter directing respondent No. 4 for sending a panel of Nikah Registrars for Ward No. 3.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Challenging the said letters the petitioner filed the Writ Petition No. 3138 of 2012 before the High Court Division and obtained Rule, but that was discharged for default on 23.01.2013.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">The writ petitioner’s further case is that by letter dated 17.11.2013 the Government appointed Mohammad Ashraf Uddin Bhuiyan (writ respondent No. 7) as Nikah Registrar for Ward No 1; by letter dated 10.11.2013 Md. Abdur Rob (writ respondent Nos. 8) was appointed as Nikah Registrar for Ward No. 2; by letter dated 10.11.2013 Md. Nazrul Islam was appointed as Nikah Registrar for Ward No. 3 and by letter dated 11.11.2013 Md. Abu Taleb was appointed as Nikah Registrar for Ward No. 4, all within Narayangonj City Corporation.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Being aggrieved, the writ petitioner filed writ petition No. 12161 of 2013 before the High Court Division and obtained Rule.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">The Rule was opposed by writ respondent Nos. 1 to 5 without filing any affidavit-in-opposition.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">After hearing the parties, upon considering the materials on record, the Rule was made absolute in part holding that the appointments made in respect of Ward Nos. 2, 3 and 4 were not illegal. However, with regard to Ward No. 1, the appointment of Md. Asraf Uddin Bhuiyan was considered to have been passed without lawful authority.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Writ respondent Md. Ashraf Uddin Bhuiyan is now before us having filed Civil Petition for Leave to Appeal No. 2901 of 2015. The Government has also challenged the impugned judgement in Civil Petition for Leave to Appeal No. 3126 of 2015. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Mr. Probir Neogi, learned Senior Advocate appearing on behalf of the leave petitioner in Civil Petition for Leave to Appeal No. 2901 of 2015 submitted that the authority concerned after following the mandatory provisions of existing law regarding appointment of temporary Nikah Registrar, drawing up a Panel of competent Nikah Registrars appointed the petitioner as temporary Nikah Registrar for Ward No. 1 of Narayangonj City Corporation, and after his appointment he has been performing his functions as Nikah Registrar to the satisfaction of the concerned authority. He further submitted that when Shiddhirgonj was merged into Narayangonj City Corporation, 5 Wards were created, and for Ward No. 1 the petitioner (Md. Ashraf Uddin Bhuiyan)was appointed and also Md. Abdur Rob, Md. Nazrul Islam and Md. Abu Taleb were appointed as temporary Nikah Registrars respectively for Ward Nos. 2, 3 and 4. He further submitted that as such, Ward No. 5 remains with the writ petitioner-respondent No. 1 herein, but the High Court Division without considering that aspect erred in declaring as unlawful the appointment of the petitioner as Nikah Registrar for Ward No. 1 under Narayangonj City Corporation. The learned Advocate further submitted that the petitioner is a resident of Mijmiji which falls within the jurisdiction of Ward No. 1, and the petitioner has been rightly appointed for that Ward. On the other hand, the records show that respondent No. 1 is a resident of Ajibpur, which is within Ward No. 5.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Mr. Biswajit Deb Nath, learned Deputy Attorney General appearing on behalf of the petitioner in Civil Petition for Leave to Appeal No. 3126 of 2015 submitted that it is within the power of the Government under the relevant law to curtail the jurisdiction of Nikah Registrars, and accordingly, Ward Nos. 1, 2, 3 and 4 of Narayangonj City Corporation have been taken away from A.S.M. Siddiqur Rahman, who was previously Kazi for Ward Nos. 1 to 5 of Narayangonj City Corporation. By furnishing a list of the incumbent Nikah Registrars of Ward Nos. 1 to 6 of Narayangonj City Corporation, he submitted that A.S.M. Siddiqur Rahman is listed as the Nikah Registrar for Ward No. 5 of Narayangonj City Corporation. He also pointed out that Md. Masihur Rahman of Sumilpara is the incumbent Nikah Registrar for Ward No. 6 of Narayangonj City Corporation. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Mr. Kamal–ul-Alam, learned Senior Advocate appearing on behalf of respondent No. 1 in both the cases made submissions in support of the impugned judgement and order of the High Court Division. He further submitted that although it is not denied that respondent No. 1 was Kazi for Ward Nos. 1 to 5 of Siddhirgonj Pourasava which merged with Narayangonj City Corporation, it is evident from the record that he is left with no jurisdiction as Nikah Registrar in any of the Wards of Narayangonj City Corporation. The learned Advocate pointed out that one Kazi Md. Masihur Rahman is the appointed Nikah Registrar for Ward Nos. 5 and 6 by appointment letter dated 22.07.2003 and he remains in that position by dint of an order of stay from the High Court Division in Writ Petition Nos. 7361 of 2011 and 620 of 2012, which is apparent from Annexure-‘K’ to the writ petition. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">We have considered the submissions of the learned Advocates appearing for the parties concerned and perused the impugned judgement of the High Court Division and other connected papers on record.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">13.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">At the outset, we should make it clear that when any person is appointed as a Nikah Registrar for any local area, his service will continue as such until and unless he is disqualified under the law. In a recent judgement by this Division in Civil Appeal Nos. 177 and 178 of 2005 (judgement delivered on 31<sup>st</sup> of May, 2016) it was observed that “upon conversion of the Union Parishad to a Pourasava only the character of the administrative unit changes.” In our view the same applies to the situation where a Pourasava becomes or is merged with a City Corporation. In the aforementioned case this Division held that after conversion the Kazi(Nikah Registrar) continues as Kazi for all the Wards of the newly created administrative unit (in this case City Corporation). He would remain the Nikah Registrar having jurisdiction over the whole of the territory for which he had been appointed as such until his jurisdiction is lawfully curtailed in respect of some or any of the Wards. Such curtailment is a power given to the Government by law, and cannot, therefore, be said to be unlawful. At the same time it must be stated that curtailment does not entail taking away all the Wards of the incumbent Nikah Registrar, thereby negating his licence altogether. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">14.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">In the impugned judgement the High Court Division observed that “as soon as the law regarding local jurisdiction has been changed those [posts] fallen (sic<em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">.)</em> vacant and respondent No. 5 has authority to issue the impugned orders.” In our view such observation is not entirely correct, inasmuch as upon getting a new administrative character (City Corporation) the posts of Nikah Registrar for the relevant Wards do not <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">ipso facto</em> become vacant. The position of Nikah Registrar for Ward Nos. 1-5 of Narayangonj City Corporation never became vacant and until the appointment of writ respondents 7-10 in Ward Nos. 1-4 of Narayangonj City Corporation, respondent No. 1 remained Nikah Registrar for all the former Wards of Siddirgonj Pourasova, i.e. Ward Nos. 1-5 of Narayangonj City Corporation. Consequently, respondent Nos. 1 never lost his position as Nikah Registrar of Ward No. 5 of Narayangonj City Corporation.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">15.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">We reiterate that a Nikah Registrar, who had been appointed as such for a number of Wards, cannot have all the wards taken away from him. The power of the Government is to curtail his jurisdiction, in other words to appoint a Nikah Registrar for any of the Wards but that power does not extend to totally eliminating his licence as Nikah Registrar, unless there is some other legitimate ground. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">16.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">               </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">From the facts of the instant case, it appears that Kazi A.S.M. Siddiqur Rahman is a resident of Ajibpur, which is within Ward No. 5 of Narayangonj City Corporation. This fact is apparent from his National I.D. Card, which was produced before us. The learned Deputy Attorney General has supplied us with a list of the incumbent Nikah Registrars of Ward Nos. 1 to 6 of Narayangonj City Corporation. It is apparent from this list that A.S.M. Siddiqur Rahman is listed as Nikah Registrar for Ward No. 5 of Narayangonj City Corporation. We also note that Md. Masihur Rahman is listed as the Nikah Registrar of Ward No. 6 of Narayangonj City Corporation, which includes Sumilpara where he lives. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">17.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">               </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">In view of the above facts and circumstances, keeping in mind that according to the Government records, the writ petitioner-respondent No. 1 herein is listed as the incumbent Nikah Registrar for Ward No. 5 of Narayangonj City Corporation, there appears to be no illegality in the appointment of the Nikah Registrars<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>for<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Ward<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Nos. 1, 2, 3 and 4. It appears from the impugned judgement that the appointment of Md. Ashraf Uddin Bhuiyan as Nikah Registrar for Ward No. 1 of Narayangonj City Corporation was declared illegal as it was claimed that he was not a resident of that Ward. However, from the records we find that said Md. Ashraf Uddin Bhuiyan, petitioner herein lives in Mijmiji, Batanpara which is within Ward No. 1 of Narayangonj City Corporation and hence, his appointment as Nikah Registrar for that Ward is not unlawful. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l2 level1 lfo3; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">18.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">               </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">We note from the additional paper book dated 05.06.2016 filed in Civil Petition for Leave to Appeal No. 2901 of 2015 that that Md. Masihur Rahman was listed as M.M.R.(Nikah Registrar) for Ward Nos. 5 and 6 under Narayangonj City Corporation. That list is dated 28.06.2015. However, that position appears to have been superseded by the list provided by the District Registrar, Narayangonj dated 12.10.2015 which is incorporated in the additional paper book dated 11.11.2015 at page 24, where Md. Masihur Rahman is listed as the Nikah Registrar of Ward No. 6 of Narayangonj City Corporation. At page 23 of the said paper book we find the name of A.S.M. Siddiqur Rahman, who is listed as Nikah Registrar for Ward No. 5 of Narayangonj City Corporation.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l2 level1 lfo3; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">19.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">               </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Thus it appears clear to us that the respondent No. 1 continues to be Nikah Registrar of Ward No. 5 of Narayangonj City Corporation. His jurisdiction in Ward Nos. 1-4 has been curtailed. Md. Masihur Rahman is the incumbent Nikah Registrar for Ward No. 6 of Narayangonj City Corporation. There is, therefore, no impediment in appointing writ respondent Nos. 7 to 10 as Nikah Registrars for Ward Nos. 1 to 4 of Narayangonj City Corporation.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l2 level1 lfo3; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">20.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">               </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">In the light of the above observations, the judgement and order of the High Court Division is modified. Since Md. Ashraf Uddin Bhuiyan is a resident of Ward No. 1 his appointment as temporary Nikah Registrar for Ward No. 1 is found to be lawful and the position of respondent No. 1 A.S.M. Siddiqur Rahman as the Nikah Registrar of Ward No. 5 of Narayangonj City Corporation, is found to be continuing.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l2 level1 lfo3; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">21.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">               </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Accordingly, with the above observations the civil petitions for leave appeal are disposed of.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.35pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Ed. </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 112%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> </span></strong></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><a href="file:///C:/Users/User/AppData/Local/Temp/Rar$DIa7196.46639/Issue__December_19__C.%20P.%202901%20of%2015__Muhammad%20Imman%20Ali_J___AD___3.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong><em><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">CIVIL PETITION FOR<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>LEAVE TO APPEAL<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>NO.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>2901 AND 3126 OF<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>2015.</span></u></em></strong></a><u> </u><span style="font-size: 9.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.2pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">(From the judgement and order dated 19<sup>th</sup> of August, 2015 passed by the High Court Division in Writ Petition No.12161 of 2013)</span></p></div></div></div></div>
821	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Most. Alhala Khatun Vs. Most. Rezia Khanam</h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> CIVIL  APPEAL  NO.  159 OF  2011   </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Muhammad Imman Ali, J.</p><p><b>Court:</b> Appellate Division ,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Abdul Quayum with Mr. A.M. Amin Uddin Senior Advocates, instructed by Syed Mahbubar Rahman Advocate-on-Record ,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2019(2) LNJ (AD)   </p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2019</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Most. Alhala Khatun:</p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Most. Rezia Khanam </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Premises Rent Control Act </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2020-03-15</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">APPELLATE DIVISION</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(CIVIL)</span></strong></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="width: 626px; margin-left: 5.4pt; border-collapse: collapse; height: 184px;" width="282"><tbody><tr style="height: 115px;"><td style="width: 258.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt; height: 115px;" valign="top"><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Muhammad Imman Ali, J</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">     </span>And</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Abu Bakar Siddiquee, J, </span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> </span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> </span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Judgment on</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">5-02-2019</span></strong></p></td><td style="width: 47.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt; height: 115px;"><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10.0pt 0in;"><a href="file:///C:/Users/User/AppData/Local/Temp/Rar$DIa7196.37237/Issue__December_19__C.%20A.%20159%20of%2011__Muhammad%20Imman%20Ali_J___AD___1.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%; font-family: Symbol; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;"><span style="mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;">}</span></span></span></a></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p></td><td style="width: 276.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt; height: 115px;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN-GB; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Most. Alhala Khatun</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">:</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: right; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">. . . Appellant.</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: center; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">-Versus-</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN-GB; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Most. Rezia Khanam</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">. .
